U.S. Loan Cotton Contract Revised; First Batch of 80,000 Bales Shipped to Shanghai; Already En Route and Arriving Soon; Stored in China Merchants Yangtze Warehouse 126

Regarding the cotton and wheat loan agreement signed between our country and the United States, except for the 320,000 tons of wheat that have already been shipped, the cotton, due to the strike in the United States that prevented loading, has had its total amount reduced from 40 million U.S. dollars to 10 million U.S. dollars after the contract was revised. Now, the first batch of loan cotton has been shipped from the United States. A reporter learned that the first batch of 80,000 bales will arrive in Shanghai soon. Preparations are being made here for warehousing and other procedures. The reporter personally went to various parties to conduct a detailed investigation. The information obtained is described in detail below.

First Batch of Cotton Shipped 127

Before the contract was revised, small batches of U.S. loan cotton shipped to Shanghai, starting from November last year to date, totaled only more than 50,000 bales. Later, the contract was revised by both parties, reducing the loan amount to 10 million U.S. dollars. The U.S. cotton will be shipped to Shanghai for another six months. The first batch shipped from the North American port of New Orleans totaled 40,000 tons, accounting for 80,000 bales, valued at 7-8 million yuan in national currency. In late May, ships were chartered and loading began. The port of New Orleans was not affected by the strike, so it was able to ship as usual.

Arriving in Shanghai in Mid-July 128

The large batch of 80,000 bales of U.S. loan cotton has been distributed among multiple ships for transport from the United States across the Pacific Ocean to Shanghai. Shanghai has received telegrams in recent days that most of the cotton-laden ships have already departed and are en route. It is expected that the first ship will arrive in port for import within three weeks. The second and third ships will follow in succession. After the U.S. cotton arrives in Shanghai this time, it must all be unloaded and stored in warehouses in Shanghai, and then purchased by households in batches. Therefore, the arrival date of the first batch of cotton in Shanghai is in mid-July, and shipments will continue to arrive in Shanghai continuously thereafter.

Stored in Yangtze Warehouse 129

The Cotton and Wheat Management Office of this port has decided to store all of the U.S. cotton in the China Merchants Bureau's Yangtze Wharf warehouse. Because the goods will arrive in Shanghai soon, Liu Hongsheng has been notified to quickly repair the warehouses at Yangtze Wharf to facilitate unloading and storage. Upon receiving this notification, Liu Hongsheng immediately sent personnel to inspect Yangtze Wharf and began work on the warehouses that needed to be repaired first. It is estimated that the repair cost will be about 4,000 yuan, which has been approved by the bureau and set a deadline for completion. At the same time, the management office of the four warehouses has also been notified to take good care of the U.S. cotton when it arrives at the wharf.

Pootung Texaco Oil Depot: All Workers Went on Strike Yesterday 130

Dagon Society reports: The Pootung Texaco Oil Depot employs over two hundred workers in the kerosene production. The day before yesterday, worker Yao Longlong, from the tinning section, arrived at the factory on time for work. However, the foreign supervisor of the department, Mr. Compson, had not yet arrived, and no soldering tin was available. Fearing delays, Yao used other soldering tin as a substitute, without significant difference. When Mr. Compson found out, instead of praising the worker, he blamed him for unauthorized use of materials and suspended him for two weeks. After repeated requests from the workers, he agreed to a three-day suspension. Unexpectedly, when the worker returned to work after the three days, Mr. Compson went back on his word and refused to reinstate him. Subsequent requests from worker representatives to the manager, "Byer," were also unsuccessful, leading to widespread indignation among all workers, who unanimously went on strike yesterday morning to show their determination. Upon learning of the Texaco workers' strike, the City Kerosene Assembly Workers' Union immediately dispatched personnel to investigate the truth. They also prepared a formal report to the Party and government authorities, requesting mediation to resolve the matter as soon as possible, to avoid affecting the workers' livelihoods. In the afternoon, they sent representatives, including He Shaozhen, to the City General Labor Union to petition for assistance. The union's General Secretary, Gong Yuting, received them and inquired in detail about the cause of the dispute. He promised to work with the Party headquarters to resolve the issue and instructed the workers to maintain order. The representatives left satisfied.

Clash Between Japanese Sailors and Western Police; Western Police Officer Burman Detained in Headquarters, Released After Negotiation by Japanese Deputy Inspector 131

At ten o'clock the night before last, four intoxicated Japanese individuals took rickshaws to the corner of Chapoo Road and Haining Road in Hongkew, in front of the Weili Grand Theatre, and alighted. When the rickshaw pullers asked for payment, the Japanese men punched them instead. A middle-aged woman, Wang Ma, happened to be passing by, and the Japanese men, for reasons unknown, suddenly turned their anger on her and assaulted her as well. A Western police officer of the Hongkew police station, British national Burman (transliteration), number 187 from the San Dao Tou precinct, arrived on patrol. Witnessing the Japanese men's behavior, he immediately advised them to stop. Not only did the Japanese men not restrain themselves, but they surrounded and attacked the Western police officer. The officer, outnumbered, was injured in the assault. The Japanese men then dispersed in a commotion. Refusing to be outdone, the officer, despite his injuries, pursued them. As he approached the vicinity of the Japanese military headquarters in Shenjiawan, a large group of Japanese soldiers gathered upon hearing the noise, blocked the Western police officer, and detained him inside the Japanese military headquarters. The martial drama came to a temporary end. Around four o'clock yesterday morning, the Western Deputy Police Chief of the Hongkew police station, Englishman Hill (transliteration), returned from an outer patrol. As he approached the side entrance of the police station, he suddenly found himself surrounded and attacked by seven or eight Japanese individuals. For self-defense, the police chief immediately drew his pistol to prevent any eventuality. Unexpectedly, the Japanese men took the opportunity to snatch the pistol

away first, then went behind the police chief and pushed him while striking him. The police chief was caught off guard and fell, injuring his knee and bleeding. Fortunately, the plainclothes Western police chief of the Hongkew police station, Robert

son, had also finished his duties and was returning home. Upon arriving at the police station and seeing Hill injured and lying on the ground, being continuously assaulted by the Japanese men, he immediately intervened. The Japanese men, thinking he was not a public official because he was in plainclothes, left Hill and went away. Hill, having suffered this unprovoked and violent act, was extremely angry. Disregarding the pain in his knee, he ran back to the police station with his bare hands, intending to seek revenge. The Chinese and Western personnel in the police station tried their best to persuade him not to act rashly to avoid any accidents. Meanwhile, a certain Japanese Deputy Inspector hurried to the Japanese military headquarters to demand the release of Burman. Initially, he was unsuccessful. Later, the Japanese Deputy Inspector returned to the Japanese Consulate and invited a certain Japanese Deputy Consul to accompany him to the headquarters. Only then was Burman released. By then, it was already dawn. Since this unfortunate incident occurred, all British individuals serving in the Shanghai Municipal Council's police department have been quite indignant. Yesterday morning, those who went to the First Special District Court to resolve cases discussed the matter amongst themselves, all saying, "We British have lost face," and a look of resentment was evident on their faces.

The Great American Evening Post reports that at ten o'clock last night, a conflict occurred between public concession police and Japanese Marines on Chapoo Road, resulting in the detention of Western police chief Bellamy by Japanese naval officers for approximately seven hours. The incident stemmed from two Japanese sailors assaulting a Chinese woman. It is said that the woman had provoked the sailors with insulting gestures, causing her to be punched in the nose and bleed profusely. A Chinese police officer, seeing this, stepped forward to intervene and attempted to arrest the two sailors. As the two resisted arrest, Western police chief Bellamy of the Hongkew police station arrived to assist the Chinese officer. At that time, a Japanese naval patrol happened to pass by and joined the argument. According to the Japanese side, Bellamy attempted to draw his pistol, but the pistol was forcibly taken away by the Japanese sailors. Subsequently, more and more Japanese people gathered, surrounding the police. Attempting to break through and call the police station for help, they were not only stopped by the Japanese sailors, but also by Japanese civilians at the scene. Another Chinese police officer blew a whistle for help, and Western police chief Ferguson responded. Seeing the situation was unfavorable and beyond his ability to handle alone, he also attempted to call the police station but was still stopped by the crowd. An American, Mr. Paige, seeing the police in a difficult situation, managed to get a phone call through to the Hongkew police station. Before long, reinforcements arrived, but the number of Japanese sailors and Marines had also greatly increased. Seeing they were outnumbered, the police agreed to go to the Chapoo Road branch of the Japanese Marines to discuss the matter. Upon arrival, both police chiefs were detained. Ferguson was released at midnight. Thereupon, two Japanese Deputy Inspectors of the Public Concession and the Police Chief of the Japanese Consulate were invited by emergency telephone call and gathered at the Chapoo Road branch. Shortly thereafter, the Superintendent of the Hongkew police station, Kennedy, and another Superintendent, Robertson, also arrived at the scene and discussed the matter for half an hour without reaching an agreement. Finally, at one thirty in the morning, they called Superintendent General Everson, who, after arriving, continued the discussion for four hours, finally releasing Bellamy at five thirty in the morning. The case seems to have come to an end. According to the Japanese side, Everson admitted that he had violated police procedure last night by drawing his pistol against the Japanese sailors before he was released. According to police procedure, this is not allowed unless one's life is in danger. When the police returned to the Hongkew police station, they were followed by a mob who wanted to assault them. They then gathered outside the police station, their demeanor menacing. The people in the police station set up a cordon around the perimeter and locked the outer doors. Later, police from the Japanese Consulate and Japanese Marines dispersed the mob, many of whom were Japanese. According to Japanese officials, the case was a minor matter and escalated due to the hot weather, causing people to be irritable. The Japanese side also implied that Western police chief Bellamy had consumed some alcohol, and those who witnessed the scene at the time could smell alcohol on Bellamy's breath. Later, someone inquired with the Superintendent's office, and the reply was that the Superintendent had no comment. As for the Japanese claim that Bellamy had drawn his pistol against the sailors and was released after admitting to drawing the pistol, the police station has neither confirmed nor denied it. However, the police station stated that they have not received any information proving Bellamy was drunk. According to an officer of the Japanese Marines, the Shanghai Municipal Council's police will hold a meeting to thoroughly investigate the case, and the Japanese Navy will also send a representative to attend. According to a Japanese news agency, this morning (the 28th), an officer of the Japanese Special Marines issued a formal statement, hoping for an early resolution to the conflict on Chapoo Road, and stated that the Marines deeply regret the occurrence of such an unfortunate incident. He also stated that Marines officers confirmed that Western police chief Bellamy had pointed a pistol at the Japanese sailors.

City Chamber of Commerce Responds: Germany Not Recalling Mark Notes; Do Not Be Fooled by Speculators 132

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce received a letter yesterday from Liu Zhuzhai of the Yixian County Chamber of Commerce in Shandong, inquiring whether the reported claims of Germany recalling Mark notes were true and whether the notes could still be used. The City Chamber of Commerce immediately replied, stating that the Mark notes issued during the German Imperial era had depreciated in value after the European War and could not be sustained. They had long been declared invalid. At the time of issuance, the Chinese Consul in Germany had sent a letter to the former General Chamber of Commerce, which published a notice advising people not to be fooled by those selling them for speculation. Many years have passed, so there is no possibility of them being recalled. Please do not believe such rumors lightly.

According to information from the International Trade Bureau, the Ministry of Industries believes that there has been no obvious progress in the export of Chinese goods. This is due to the global financial recession and the lack of improvement by the Chinese. Fresh Pork Vendors Association Requests Withdrawal of Contract System and Announcement of Original Tax Rate of 0.5% for Pork Business Tax in Jiangbei 136

The original tax rate for the pork business tax in Jiangbei was set at 0.5%. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance suddenly changed it to 1%, inviting bids for a contract system. Chen Shichu won the contract, changing the tax to 20 cents per pig. Pork merchants Xu Bomou, Chen Zimin, Liu Wenfu, Yang Zhengxiang, etc., sent a letter requesting the Shanghai Fresh Pork Vendors Association to seriously negotiate. The association's executive committee believed that the matter involved illegal exactions and should be reported to the authorities for correction. The original telegram is excerpted below: To President Wang of the Executive Yuan, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, and Chairman Chen of the Jiangsu Provincial Government: The Jiangbei counties of Jiangsu Province's pork business tax, previously approved by the Ministry of Finance (your ministry), was to be handled according to the precedent of Anhui Province's collection through agents, charging business tax at a rate of 0.5% of the business amount for both vendors and preserved meat businesses, without counting the number of pigs in the hold or collecting the tax per pig. The Ministry-set tax rate of 0.5% is already clear. Recently, the National Financial Conference proposed five measures to rectify the business tax system. The third measure, on industry classification limits and taxation standards, stated that the first category, merchandise sales, (a) ordinary daily necessities, should be taxed at 0.5%. Selling pigs also falls under the category of daily necessities, making the tax rate of 0.5% even clearer. Furthermore, the fourth measure stated that business tax should not be levied on goods themselves but should be levied on employment, not on goods, which would be akin to levying transit duties. Existing methods such as collection through commercial associations, inviting bids for contracts, and sharing the tax among businesses easily lead to abuses and should be thoroughly reformed in each locality. The regulations are strict and the measures are excellent. However, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance suddenly changed the pork business tax in the Jiangbei counties from 0.5% to 1%, altering the method and inviting bids for a contract. Chen Shichu won the contract and set up offices along the routes of each county in the guise of Jiangbei Pork Business Tax Commissioners, advising pork boats to dock and counting the pigs in the hold to tax them at 20 cents per pig. They also collect inspection fees for the tickets along the way. Any slight non-compliance results in detention. Because the pork merchants know that pigs are perishable goods, if they are detained and delayed, they risk death. Therefore, they can only painfully pay the tax. However, the tax tickets still state that the tax is being collected at 1% of the principal. The deceitfulness of this tactic is self-evident. According to the Jiangbei market price, each pig is valued at only about 10 yuan. Taxing 20 cents per pig exceeds the Ministry-set tax rate several times. At a time when commerce is declining and the rural economy is collapsing, and when maintaining and restoring it is already precarious, such illegal and oppressive measures will inevitably cause merchants to hesitate and farmers to stop raising pigs. The impact will be unthinkable. The contract system has serious drawbacks. In order to win the bid, contractors offer high prices. Once they win the bid, they disregard the law and are oblivious to the big picture. They only know to extract as much as possible, arbitrarily and oppressively. The so-called losing in the east and gaining in the west only increases the burden on pork merchants, accelerating rural bankruptcy. We earnestly implore you to care about the people's plight and sympathize with the merchants' difficulties. We urgently request that you order the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance to withdraw the contract system and issue a clear order announcing that the pork business tax is 0.5%, and that no oppressive collections should be allowed in violation of the order, in order to alleviate the merchants' difficulties and maintain the people's livelihood. We anxiously await your command. Shanghai Fresh Pork Vendors Association, respectfully.

Communist Party Member Zhou Xiancheng's Declaration of Surrender 139

Central News Agency reports: Communist Party member Zhou Xiancheng (pseudonym Lao Cao), a native of Suzhou, Anhui, is 29 years old. Moved by patriotic enthusiasm due to the national crisis of the September 18th Incident and angered by the partial phenomena and personal dissatisfaction at the time, he joined the Communist Party after the January 28th Incident through the introduction of Li Jinsheng and was assigned to a street branch. He successively served as a propaganda officer for the Communist Workers' Union, an organization affairs officer for the Jiangsu Provincial Committee, a propaganda officer, a provincial committee inspector, and an internal transport officer for the Provincial Standing Committee. A week ago, he was transferred from transport work to the position of Party Secretary of the General Command of the British-American Strike. He had just started working when he was arrested. After being persuaded and guided, he suddenly realized the truth and surrendered, issuing a declaration saying: "I am an intellectual who has lived in the Communist Party for nearly three years. During the work process, I often felt disappointment and hit walls, deeply understanding that the Communist Party is an obstacle to the national united front. In my recent arrest, I was sincerely persuaded and analyzed by several amiable and kind advanced comrades regarding the current reality of China. I have even more clearly realized that the Communist Party's politics are on the wrong path. The theory of class struggle is not suitable for an industrially backward China, just as one pharmacy cannot cure different diseases. The core of the Communist Party advocates class struggle, believing that class interests outweigh national interests, thus forcibly creating classes in China and causing them to harm each other, giving imperialists the opportunity to benefit. Therefore, during the War of Resistance against Japan, the Communist Party provoked non-cooperation between officers and soldiers, disrupted the rear, seized cities, and expanded bandit areas, implementing separation. Such a frantic Communist Party has made mistakes and conspiracies that undermine the national united front. Therefore, especially since the September 18th Incident, the Communist Party's organization has been collapsing day by day, and the people's faith has been disappearing day by day. The atmosphere of self-reflection has formed an unstoppable trend, from individual to whole batches. In short, the Communist Party is reaching the final stage of its demise. What China needs most now is a unified national front to fight against domestic and foreign feudalism and imperialism, and to implement the Three People's Principles revolution so that the nation can be revived. Now that Xiancheng has discovered the bright path and the truth of the revolution, he vows to serve under the leadership of the Chinese Kuomintang, uphold the Three People's Principles, and strive for the national revival movement. He is willing to do everything in his power to eliminate the Communist Party, eradicate all reactionary forces, and seek the survival and liberation of the Chinese nation. He also hopes that young people who have gone astray will humbly reflect on their mistakes, quickly realize the truth, and strive toward the bright and true path of the Three People's Principles."

Heatwave Persists in Shanghai; Emergency Hospitals Established Early 145

The weather has been extremely hot in various regions recently, particularly in our city. Temperatures have consistently reached over 100 degrees, even reaching 98 or 99 degrees indoors. The drought and stifling humidity are causing widespread discomfort. The heat persisted yesterday, with a high of 101.5 degrees, only half a degree lower than the previous day. Preparations for epidemic prevention work are essential and should be made as early as possible.

Epidemic Prevention Hospitals Established on the 1st 146

The hot weather in the city has led many residents to consume cold foods, often neglecting hygiene. As a result, there have been several cases of seasonal illnesses. Yesterday, there were more than a dozen cases of dysentery, all of whom sought medical treatment. Fortunately, there have been no cases of cholera. Recognizing the sudden change in climate and the increasing number of sick residents, all emergency hospitals plan to establish operations earlier than scheduled, with a target date of the first of next month.

Over Ten Thousand Inoculations Daily 147

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, the Public Concession's Health Department, and the French Concession's Health Department have been intensifying their inoculation efforts due to the high number of seasonal illnesses. All three areas have dispatched personnel to schools, factories, organizations, and communities to administer preventative injections. Over ten thousand people are being inoculated daily, with yesterday's total exceeding 13,000.

Health Bureau Conducts Testing 148

Following the increase in inoculation efforts, the demand for vaccines at the Health Bureau's Health Testing Laboratory has surged. The laboratory is currently rushing to produce more vaccines to meet the need. According to the director of the laboratory, Cheng Shuzhen, in an interview with the Huadong News Agency, the laboratory will produce approximately 30,000 to 40,000 bottles of vaccine this year, sufficient for two million people. Furthermore, with the emergency hospitals scheduled to open on the first of next month, the laboratory will dispatch specialists to test the stool samples of patients in the emergency hospitals to detect any cases of cholera.

Shanghai Women Love "Nature"; 1.11 Million Yuan Spent in Five Months; Mostly on Perfumes, Powders, Jewelry, and Cosmetics; May Imports Total 300,500 Yuan 149

[This refers only to imported goods; domestic products are not included]

Last year, imports of perfumes and powders reached over 1.5 million yuan. From January to April of this year, they reached 520,000 yuan, mostly consumed by women in the Shanghai area. This astounding figure is shocking. A Datong News Agency reporter learned from the International Trade Bureau yesterday morning that perfume imports in May reached 213,985 yuan, surpassing previous figures. This demonstrates that Shanghai women are not showing any restraint. However, the aforementioned figures only cover perfumes and powders. The import of foreign cosmetics and real and imitation jewelry is also substantial. In May, imports of cosmetics totaled 63,508 yuan, and imports of real and imitation jewelry totaled 27,720 yuan. Therefore, the total import value of women's goods in May was 300,513 yuan. Looking at the import figures for women's goods over the past five months of this year, perfumes and powders totaled 747,627 yuan, cosmetics totaled 229,610 yuan, and real and imitation jewelry totaled 136,240 yuan, bringing the total to 1,113,477 yuan. This clearly demonstrates that Shanghai women's love of "nature" is truly captivating.

Epidemic Rampant in Western Shanghai; Three Family Members Die 150

Liu Changsu, a 52-year-old man from Taizhou, had three sons and one daughter. The eldest son, Guosheng, was 13 years old; the second son, Agou, was 8 years old; and the youngest son, Yukou, was 6 years old. His daughter, Asi, was only 3 years old. The entire family lived on a houseboat in the Fahua River near Tongren Bridge in Xujiahui Town, western Shanghai. Recently, due to the hot weather, Yukou suddenly contracted measles and died within a few hours. Unexpectedly, Guosheng and Agou also contracted the same illness. Initially, they suffered abdominal pain and vomiting, followed by a burning fever. Changsu, lacking the means for medical treatment, only gave them two bottles of herbal medicine water, but the medicine had no effect, and their condition worsened. Unable to provide further assistance, the two brothers died one after another yesterday morning around 10 AM, causing great sorrow for the family. They were finally laid to rest in the evening.

Suzhou Opera Singer Sues Again; Grandson of Li Hongzhang; Files Lawsuit to Confirm Identity 151

Zhao Peiying (also known as Fan Zhenzhen), a local woman who works as a Suzhou opera singer, was previously involved with Li Shiquan, a grandson of Li Hongzhang. Their relationship soured, and Zhao sued Li for enticement. The trial resulted in Li being acquitted, and the verdict was upheld after three appeals. More recently, Zhao sued Li for abandoning their child, but then suddenly withdrew the lawsuit. These events have been previously reported in detail in this newspaper. Now, because Li consistently denies having lived with Zhao and absolutely denies that the child is his, Zhao has hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the Civil Division of the First Special District Court against Li to confirm his identity. Once his identity is confirmed, she will pursue further litigation. Judge Qiao Wanxuan summoned the parties for questioning in the Civil Court 7 yesterday afternoon and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Naval Aviation Plant

Self-Made Moth Aircraft Completed Yesterday; Soon to Undertake a National Long-Distance Maiden Flight; Piloted by Instructor Xu Chengqi 152

The Navy Aviation Plant has completed the construction of its self-made Moth steel-framed training aircraft after more than two months of work. According to sources at the plant, the aircraft will soon undertake a national long-distance maiden flight. The construction process of the aircraft is detailed below.

Motivation for Construction: The construction of the steel-framed Moth training aircraft was motivated by the fact that after the Jiangfeng training and reconnaissance aircraft was converted into a seaplane, there was a shortage of training aircraft for students. The Aviation Plant drafted a plan that was approved by the Naval Department for construction. The cost of the aircraft is approximately 15,000 yuan, similar to that of the Ninghai.

Aircraft Structure: The Moth aircraft is a biplane with a waterborne design. The fuselage is silver-gray, the frame is sturdy, and the exterior is attractive. It has a payload of 766 kilograms and seats two people. It can fly for seven hours with a range of 896 kilometers.

Long-Distance Flight: The aircraft is scheduled to undergo a test flight in early next month. After a thorough inspection of the components, it will begin its national long-distance maiden flight. The pilot will be instructor Xu Chengqi, who previously attempted a long-distance flight with the Jiangfeng but was unsuccessful.

Ministry of Communications Instructs Subordinates; Courteous Service for Customers; Violators Punished According to Severity 153

The Ministry of Communications issued an instruction to the Postal Administration, International Telecommunications Bureau, Telephone Bureau, Telecommunications Administration, Radio Station, Postal Savings and Remittances Administration, Telegraph Bureau, Long-Distance Telephone Administration, China Merchants Bureau, and China and Eurasia Airlines, stating: "Upon investigation, employees of all state-run agencies under the Ministry must be courteous, humble, and sincere in their interactions with Chinese and foreign individuals, and must not act arrogantly or neglectfully. This instruction was issued to all agencies in March of this year. However, it has recently come to our attention that a few employees have deeply ingrained habits and have failed to correct their behavior. It must be understood that courtesy is essential in human interaction, especially in China, which is known as a nation of etiquette. Public servants should strive to 'serve the people' as their mission, and state-owned enterprises should be subject to government supervision and guidance, with the people as the focus, as sovereignty resides with the people. From a business perspective, those who come are customers and must be treated with the utmost respect. All employees should understand this principle deeply. As the New Life Movement is being implemented nationwide, all civil servants must correct their behavior if they have shortcomings, and strive to be a role model for society. In the future, any such misconduct that interferes with business is a minor matter, but it will have a significant impact on the government's credibility. Strict rectification is necessary to maintain discipline. Therefore, we reiterate this order to the heads of all agencies, requiring them to pay special attention to the attitude of all employees towards Chinese and foreign individuals. Any cases of arrogance or disrespect should be immediately punished according to the severity of the offense. The Ministry will also dispatch personnel to conduct thorough inspections at any time. If the heads of agencies fail to report such incidents or engage in concealment, the Ministry will also impose penalties. In addition to separate orders, we hereby instruct the bureau to relay this order to all employees, requiring them to strictly comply without fail."

Liang Chengyu Sentenced to Life Imprisonment, Liang Still Declares Appeal 178

Liang Chengyu, the former Chinese detective of the No. 2 General Police Station, was accused of kidnapping Li Huiqing and Lu Shifan and demanding ransom. The Northern Changsheng Guildhall Announces the Reasons for Not Holding a General Meeting 179

The foreign clothing industry in this city has traditionally had the Northern Changsheng Guildhall, located at the Lower Hai Temple on Tangshan Road. In the past, the directors took turns serving as head officers. Recently, party and government organs appointed industry leaders to organize a reorganization committee to start restructuring to comply with new laws and regulations and to revitalize the business. However, the reorganization has been going on for a long time, with many disputes and obstacles preventing the convening of a general meeting. The committee recently issued a public notice, which will be widely published in various newspapers in the coming days. Here is the original text: "This association was ordered to reorganize the Northern Changsheng Guildhall. The progress has been reported in the Shen, Xin, Chen, and Min newspapers in May. We originally intended to convene an election meeting as soon as possible to carry out the handover. However, the organization department only handed over the newly compiled list of members, but the old eight ledgers and account books of this guildhall have not yet been submitted to the association, making it impossible for the association to verify them. Therefore, the matter has been delayed. This association has now submitted a request to the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, ordering the reorganization committee members Wang Jiliang and Wu Fuji to submit the old regulations and eight account books to the bureau for verification. In addition to instructing Wang and Wu to comply with the order, we expect to convene a general meeting in the near future. We are deeply concerned that members may not understand the truth, so we hereby announce the above. Chairman of the Committee: Xu Shanchang. Standing Committee Members: Wang Fuchen, Zhang Baofu."

The Wusong 7th District Precinct Captures Armed Hooligans 180

Yao Benyuan, the chief of the Wusong 7th District Precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, learned on the afternoon of the 27th of this month that over a hundred Guangdong hooligans, who usually resided in Shanghai, were carrying a large number of weapons, including explosives, bayonets, iron bars, iron whips, and nitric acid, and were intending to attack Zhang Yucheng, a worker in the factory. Fortunately, Chief Yao Benyuan discovered it early and prevented a major disaster. He arrested the leaders, Li Niubo and Zhuo Xue, and over twenty of their accomplices, including Chen Hua, and took them to the precinct for questioning. They made cunning excuses. Chief Yao believed that the case involved gathering a crowd to commit violence with weapons, which would disrupt public order, and submitted a report with witnesses to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for further investigation.

Two Routes Ban Stray Dogs From Entering Stations 181

The stations along the two railway lines are mostly located in rural areas, and stray dogs often break into the stations. Not only are the dogs dirty, which is unsightly, but their excrement on the ground also hinders cleanliness. If they bite passengers or if rabid dogs spread rabies, it would seriously affect the railway service. The bureau, emphasizing hygiene, has instructed the traffic department and the police department to strictly ban them from entering the stations.

Chen Hanqiang Returns to China to Teach Western Boxing 182

Mr. Chen Hanqiang has lived in Australia since childhood and is proficient in Western boxing. He has participated in boxing matches in that country for 21 years, competing with world-renowned boxers over 400 times. Except for three defeats, Chen won all the other matches. It is truly commendable for a Chinese to achieve such an honor abroad. Chen has held the top position in Australian boxing five times and won the Victoria Prize in 1929, regarded as the top lightweight in Australia. Now, to serve his motherland, he has returned to China to impart his skills to the Chinese people. Last week, he gave a demonstration for reporters from the North-China Daily News and others, and the audience praised him endlessly. He is currently employed by the Jingwu Athletic Association and teaches at both the Yokohama Bridge and the Mainland Emporium. Many Chinese and foreigners have signed up. This Saturday, he will also give a performance at the Central Auditorium.

Pan Lanshi Memorial Service to be Held at Lake Society on July 1st 183

Pan Lanshi, a poet from Lingnan, passed away more than two months ago. His funeral arrangements were handled entirely by his friends and students, and his son has never been heard from. Therefore, it was not possible to issue an obituary or hold a funeral. Now, his friends Ye Gongchuo, Wu Tiecheng, Xia Jiancheng, Yao Yuqin, Lu Danlin, Feng Wenfeng, and Tan Jingtang An, among others, have initiated a memorial service to be held at the Lake Society on Guizhou Road from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM on July 1st. A notice has been issued. Those who wish to send condolences should use cash and send it to Jin Songqing at the China Arts and Crafts Hall, 692 Hankou Road, to help the widow and orphans. Pan's last couplet, for the Small Collection of Jian Song Pavilion, the Peach Blossom Appreciation Poem, is appended below: "Last night, both feet were clear this morning (Lan), baby orioles and swallows all rejoice (Dong), the spring scenery in the small garden urges the guest's dream (Zhuang), looking at the flowers under the moon, the eyes are brighter (Jin). A branch of scarlet peach in the courtyard is like red snow (Lan), as if one were in Heyang City (An). Where is the otherworldly flower source of apricot (Dong)? The east wind blows the shadow across the window (Jin). It is rare to hold a cup and enjoy together (Qu), happily listening to the flute, dreaming of three lives (Zhuang)." The sound of fading ridicule seems to have foreknowledge.

Incoming Correspondence: The Functions of the Salt Affairs Auditing Office and its Relationship to Reorganizing Salt Affairs 195

During the years 1934 and 1935, official systems were established. The central government set up the Salt Affairs Bureau and the General Auditing Office, both under the Ministry of Finance. Each salt-producing area had a Salt Transport Commissioner, Deputy Commissioner, and branch auditing offices. Each salt-selling area had a Salt Monopoly Bureau and an auditing office, or a tax collection bureau, separately subordinate to the Salt Affairs Bureau and the General Auditing Office. Thus, salt affairs were divided into two major parts, separated into administration and auditing. The administrative organs were in charge of matters related to field production, transportation, sales, and anti-smuggling. The auditing organs were in charge of matters related to collecting salt taxes, weighing and releasing salt, and compiling reports. This not only created redundant structures but also caused many constraints. It not only wasted expenses but also greatly hindered the reorganization of salt affairs. Fundamentally, it was already a mistake. The biggest reasons for this were two-fold:

From the perspective of political principles, the main purpose of salt administration is tax collection. If there were no salt tax, what salt affairs would there be? Salt is produced in the fields and sold on the shore. Its source is entirely in production, and its destination is entirely in sales. "There must be annual production for annual sales, and only then can there be annual sales tax." If there is no place to sell the salt, where does the tax come from? The key to production and sales lies entirely in transportation. No matter who wants to transport salt, they must pay taxes according to regulations before it can be weighed and released. Salt with tax is called official salt, and salt without tax is called smuggled salt. If the official cannot defeat the smuggled, tax revenue will be lost. Preventing smuggling depends on anti-smuggling. Anti-smuggling is for protecting taxes. Therefore, field affairs, transportation affairs, and anti-smuggling affairs are all established for tax affairs. The root of salt tax lies entirely in field production and transportation and sales. The matter is very complex, and it is best to have specialists. It is completely different from ordinary tax collection. Therefore, tax affairs and administrative affairs cannot be absolutely separated. This is the first mistake.

From the perspective of the history of official systems, China's salt affairs have had special officials since the Han and Tang dynasties. In the Han dynasty, the Grand Minister of Agriculture was in charge of salt affairs, which was the beginning of salt affairs belonging to the Ministry of Finance. (In the Han system, the Grand Minister of Agriculture's duties were like those of today's Minister of Finance. Under the Grand Minister of Agriculture, an independent organization was formed, with a Salt Commissioner in charge of national salt affairs.) In the Song dynasty, the Left Secretary of the Ministry of Revenue was in charge of checking salt taxes to understand their increase and decrease, which was the beginning of salt affairs auditing. (In the Song system, the Ministry of Revenue was in charge of checking the amount of national salt tax, which is the function of today's auditing office. "Checking" is the earliest term for auditing.) From the Ming and Qing dynasties onwards, each province's salt taxes were audited by the Ministry of Revenue, which is how the name of auditing originated. Since the Song dynasty, the highest administrative organ in the central government has been in charge of auditing matters. All production and sales figures were subject to auditing, not just tax revenue. Auditing salt tax was an important administrative task. In the early years of the Republic of China, forcibly dividing production, sales, transportation, and anti-smuggling into administrative affairs was already far from the principles of the official system. This is another mistake.

Reorganizing salt affairs was originally intended to eliminate accumulated malpractices and increase tax revenue. However, because the division of powers was fundamentally flawed, all issues related to the rectification of field production, the transformation of transportation and sales, and the improvement of anti-smuggling are closely related to the collection of salt taxes. The auditing side must consult with the administrative side. However, matters related to administration should be handled by the administrative organs. But administrative personnel are limited by bad habits, content with corruption, or vehemently opposed due to differences in opinion, disputes over authority, or greed for kickbacks. They may even outwardly agree but secretly sabotage. Often, the obstruction of one matter leads to many obstacles for the whole. Although it is said that during the years 1934, 1935, and 1936, the auditing side was determined to make progress on reorganization issues, and tax revenue increased year by year, achieving some results, the lack of unified authority made progress difficult. Everything was handled piecemeal, and there was never a complete reform.

In 1931, it was recognized that anti-smuggling affairs were related to tax revenue and should be reorganized urgently. Therefore, in March of that year, they were placed under the jurisdiction of the General and Branch Auditing Offices. After taking over, the existing anti-smuggling troops were reorganized into tax police, and the regimental system was changed to a district system. Serious rectification and strict training were carried out. The various bad habits of previous anti-smuggling efforts were gradually eliminated, and the investigation of smuggled salt was quite effective. In 1932, it was also recognized that the reorganization of salt affairs required unified authority and the elimination of accumulated malpractices, as well as the elimination of redundant personnel and the reduction of expenses. Therefore, in July of that year, the administrative organs were reorganized so that auditing personnel would also hold administrative positions. After taking over, the first step was to strictly eliminate all kinds of existing corrupt practices. In fact, the biggest malpractice on the administrative side was the collection of kickbacks. The corruption of salt administration was also due to this. Now that authority is unified, the reorganization of field production, transportation, and sales is carried out simultaneously, aiming to achieve a complete reform. Although it has not been long since the concurrent management began, the results are already considerable. In 1929, tax revenue was 85 million yuan. In 1933, it increased to 159 million yuan. If the three northeastern provinces were included, it would be 184 million yuan, more than double compared to 1929 (see attached Table 1).

Whether the auditing office concurrently manages salt administration and anti-smuggling has a significant relationship with the increase in tax revenue. The eleven districts where the auditing office concurrently managed salt administration and anti-smuggling saw an increase of over 21 million yuan in tax revenue compared to 1931 and 1933, while the eight districts where the auditing office did not concurrently manage saw an increase of only over 2 million yuan (see attached Table 2).

After the auditing office concurrently managed administration, the administrative expenses of each district were greatly reduced. The administrative expenses of the eleven districts of Huainan, Huaibei, Songjiang, Liangzhe, Shandong, Fujian, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Hunan, and Jiangxi in 1931 were 2.8 million yuan. After the administrative merger, the budget for 1933 was reduced to 730,000 yuan. In comparison, there was a reduction of 2.15 million yuan (see attached Table 3). However, as mentioned above, the tax revenue of these eleven districts increased by over 21 million yuan compared to 1931 and 1933. The tax revenue of the eight districts where the auditing office did not concurrently manage administration in 1933 was 43 million yuan, only one-third of the eleven districts where the auditing office concurrently managed administration (the tax revenue of the eleven districts was 115 million yuan), while the administrative expenses were four times higher (in 1933, the administrative expenses of the eight districts that did not concurrently manage administration were 2.83 million yuan, while the eleven districts that concurrently managed administration were 730,000 yuan (see attached Table 4)). For example, the expenses of the Guangdong district's transportation commissioner's office alone reached 750,000 yuan per year, exceeding the total administrative expenses of the eleven districts that concurrently managed administration. If one does not want to reorganize salt affairs, then so be it. If one wants to reorganize salt affairs, increase revenue, reduce expenditure, and eliminate accumulated malpractices, salt administration should naturally be merged into the auditing office.

Since the auditing office concurrently managed the administration of eleven districts, the reduction in administrative expenses has been as described above. The auditing expenses of the auditing office itself have also decreased without increasing:

1931: 8,431,000 yuan

1932: 8,000,000 yuan

1933: 7,321,000 yuan

Comparing the expenses of the auditing office itself with tax revenue, it only accounts for slightly more than 4%, which is also less than the auditing office in the Beijing era (see attached diagram).

Before the auditing office concurrently managed anti-smuggling in the eleven districts of Shandong, Huaibei, Huainan, Songjiang, Liangzhe, Hubei, Hunan, Anhui, Jiangxi, Henan, and Fujian, there were over 21,000 officials and police officers in 1929, with annual expenses of over 3.81 million yuan. After the auditing office concurrently managed, in 1933, the number of officials and police officers was reduced to over 15,000, with expenses of 3.91 million yuan. In comparison, the number of people decreased, but expenses increased. This was due to improving the treatment of police officers to encourage integrity. However, based on the experience of recent years, the number of anti-smuggling personnel and expenses must be increased in order to increase the effectiveness of anti-smuggling. After the construction of warehouses and the management of field affairs in each district are perfected in the future, the anti-smuggling police force and expenses can be greatly reduced.

In summary, the reorganization of salt affairs is to increase tax revenue. The first step is to eliminate accumulated malpractices. Moreover, from the perspective of political principles and the history of official systems, the key to salt affairs is tax collection, and auditing tax revenue is an important administrative task. The so-called field production, transportation, sales, and anti-smuggling are all matters that the auditing organs should handle. How can redundant organs be established outside the auditing office? What should be urgently corrected is that now that the specialized merchant system has not been abolished, the name of the administrative organ still exists. It should be merged and further reformed.

Chunqiu

Fragrant and Vague Records of the Imperial Palace 196

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

So what exactly were the "main courses," numbering a hundred, and the "snacks," numbering forty or fifty? I really can't give you a detailed answer! Because there were really too many varieties of dishes eaten in the palace, and even in the carts there were quite a few, so it's definitely not something that ordinary people can remember. I said earlier that Chinese food is a "practical science" with a very wide scope, so how could I possibly remember so much?

Let me give a few examples: For example, clear-stewed fat duck was a dish that the Empress Dowager loved to eat very much. The way it was cooked was to first remove the feathers and liver from the duck, wash it clean, and then add some seasonings, and put it in a porcelain jar; then put this porcelain jar in an iron pot filled with half clear water, tightly cover the pot to prevent the air from escaping, and just let it simmer on low heat for three days in a row, so that the duck is completely tender, so tender that you don't need to cut it with a knife, you just need to use chopsticks to pick it up, and you can easily break it open. Then you can feast on it! Although the Empress Dowager sometimes picked up some duck meat to eat, she mostly picked up the duck skin to eat; because that layer of duck skin was the most exquisite and delicious part of this dish.

In addition to the clear-stewed fat duck, the following dishes were also commonly found on the Empress Dowager's table, and were also some of her favorites.

Smoked and roasted things seemed to suit the Empress Dowager's taste the most, like roast duck, roast suckling pig, smoked chicken, braised lamb leg, etc., which were almost constantly being served. These things are certainly not rare items, and ordinary people can enjoy them in restaurants outside, but the cooking method in the palace is generally more elaborate than outside. According to the Empress Dowager herself, the dish she loved to eat the most when she was young was roast pork skin. The way it was cooked was to first cut the pork with skin into small square pieces, and then fry them in lard, until the skin on the meat was crispier than anything else, and its taste was really enough to make people drool. (70)

A Woman's Buttons 197

— Sharp

The Jiangxi Provincial Government, acting on the orders of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, has formulated measures to ban women's strange and unusual clothing, with detailed regulations on women's attire; but it does not mention the button issue on cheongsams.

The number of buttons on a woman's cheongsam is countless, and I can't say the exact number. Because none of my female friends are willing to let me count them slowly. Although there are often women standing and watching outside the display windows of large companies, I sometimes want to pay attention and count, but I am nearsighted and have slow vision, and often when I am about to finish counting, she leaves again. So I have long wanted to count the number of buttons on a woman's cheongsam, but I can never fulfill my wish. A friend (of course, a male friend) told me that he counted seventeen pairs of buttons on a certain lady's cheongsam, and his eyesight is better than mine, so he is probably not wrong.

The function of buttons is simply to prevent clothes from loosening, and six pairs are enough for our men's long gowns. Why must there be as many as seventeen pairs? Moreover, if a tailor makes more buttons, it will cost more effort, and the wages will increase accordingly. The price of a single shirt is as high as three or four yuan, which has a great impact on the wearer's own material resources! Also, it takes a lot of time to button and unbutton them when wearing. I think that in today's complex society, we should standardize the things we use by simplifying them, and use the time saved to do something beneficial. Like Japanese clothing, it is finished with just a belt. Westerners also don't have many buttons, which may also express their national character, not willing to waste time.

Ming Xie Jin's poem "On the Buttons of Palace Women" is quite humorous. It is recorded as follows: "A piece of silk gauze cut from plain silk; the beauty's figure surpasses Chang'e. If the spring heart is willing to be locked up firmly, why use so many buttons?" I don't know if the women of today like to have more buttons because they want to firmly lock up the spring heart.

Old Tales of Goldfish 198

— Yan Qiao

Raising goldfish is indeed a very poetic hobby. My old friends Shou Juan and Ji Ren both have a goldfish addiction. Shou Juan even matches the fish's form and color with the names of ci poem patterns, which is even more interesting.

Song Yue Ke's Cheng Shi says: "Today, there are fish farmers in Zhongdu who can change fish to golden color, crucian carp are the best, followed by carp. Wealthy nobles often carefully dig stone to make ponds, placing them between the eaves and windows for enjoyment. When asked about the technique, they secretly refuse to tell. Some say that feeding ordinary fish with small red worms purchased from the market for a hundred days will make them all like this, first white like silver, then gradually yellow, and after a long time golden. I have not had time to verify whether it is true or not." This passage is too unscientific. Golden crucian carp and golden carp have their own seeds, and they will definitely not change color by eating small red worms. It also says: "When Ni Xi returned to Sichuan, he drew lake water and floated it on three giant ships to follow, with strange and magnificent appearances, not just two kinds." Xi was Qin Hui's son. Carrying fish from Hangzhou to Sichuan on giant ships can be considered a fish-loving addiction, unmatched throughout the ages.

Goldfish are seen in odes and poems. Su Zimei's "Leaning on the Pine Bridge, I Tap it and Watch the Golden Crucian Carp, Lingering Alone All Day Long." Su Dongpo's "I Know the Goldfish of Nanping." Before that, there were probably more, but I have not seen them.

Xiang Lian Lou's diary says: "Zuo Jigaofu raised a tank of goldfish, using the number of offspring as a sign of the prosperity of his disciples, a year with many offspring, his father would count and say that so-and-so should enter school, but not Jigaofu. Zuo was nine years old, very angry, and took advantage of the gap to kill all the fish in the tank. When his father questioned him, he replied with the truth." Treating goldfish as a tortoise shell for divination of the success of his disciples is also a strange idea. That young master, believing it to be true, vented his anger on the fish, which is even more bizarre. It is a great misfortune for goldfish to have such an encounter. Jigaofu's words and deeds throughout his life were somewhat spicy, and there is already a hint of it here.

These days, the south is experiencing the plum rain season, and the torturous period for goldfish has arrived. If you are not careful, they will get sick. The goldfish market in the old capital is very prosperous. There is no plum rain season there, so they probably won't be tortured by the yellow plum weather. In the year I first arrived in Suzhou, I also raised a tank of goldfish, and they were all sacrificed to the yellow plum weather within two or three days. So Zuo Jigaofu can be said to have a yellow plum temper, haha!

Dangerous Small Boat 199

— Dongzhu

Military reduction fails, world peace, countries expand armaments

The Movement and Stillness of Paintings 200

— Zheng Yimei

Although I can't paint, I quite like to talk about painting theory with several friends who are painters. The other day, I met Mr. Tao Lengyue at a banquet. Not only has he reached a high peak in technique, but his theoretical aspect is also quite developed. He said: "Ordinary people often use the words 'vivid' and 'lively' to praise paintings, but in fact, stillness is better than movement, and the skill of stillness is better than movement. Therefore, to use an idiom, it can be said that it is better to be still than to move. Moreover, people's hearts are still not tired of chaos, and the great war is imminent. When the time comes, the lives of the people will be devastated, and the material losses will be unimaginable. Then, this murderous intent is hidden in the word 'movement.' If we then add fuel to the fire between silk and plain, making the prelude to movement, this is absolutely impossible. Therefore, my paintings are always a cool moon, silently illuminating the mountains and rivers, causing people to silently contemplate and dispel all thoughts of fame, profit, contention, and contention, as if using still paintings to pray for world peace." I couldn't help but agree with him after hearing this theory.

He once traveled far to Sichuan last year, and took a detour through the seven lakes of Xiaoxiang, climbing Mount Heng of Southern Yue. Because his paintings are mostly scenes of quiet nights with bright moons, he spent the night on the banks of the Jialing River and at the top of Mount Zhurong, completing dozens or hundreds of drafts. This time, he held an exhibition at the YMCA in the Eight Immortals Bridge, and Chinese and Western people all admired it, which shows that the help of the landscape is not only true for Sima's writing.

Four Northeast Company Commanders 201

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 31: Three Battles, White-Clad Men Charge Through the Snow Formation, the Entire Battalion Dies for their Country, Red-Eyed Men Enter the Gun Forest

Zi Qiang led his brothers into the ravine, and the sun had already turned a ghastly red, setting west over the mountain peaks. The ravine was gloomy and cold, and a chill attacked them. Everyone walked in the snow, their feet completely buried in it. No one spoke, only the sound of footsteps pulling and stepping in the snow, which added to the silence of the environment. Zi Qiang walked to a protruding cliff and called his brothers to shrink to the bottom of the cliff together. This was a sheltered place, and although there were still a few inches of snow on the ground, there was no wind cutting into their skin, which made them feel much more comfortable. The brothers had always only known to obey orders, where to go, what to do, was not allowed to be asked. So at this time, the brothers followed Zi Qiang's orders and entered the bottom of the protruding cliff together. Everyone thought, why abandon such good fortifications in the fortress and run into this ravine? And now there is not a ghost of the enemy in sight, why hide like this? But the commander's orders are correct, and no one can outwardly show a suspicious attitude. It was also at this time that Zi Qiang suddenly showed a tense attitude, shouting repeatedly: Lie down! Lie down! Everyone had walked with great difficulty in the deep snow to get here, and was really a little tired. Having the opportunity to rest, the ranks were also scattered. At this time, hearing the order to lie down, they also knew that danger was coming. Everyone lay down in the snow in a flurry. Zhao Ziqiang himself, regardless of the depth of the snow, also lay down with them. Because after the company commander lay down, he didn't make any noise, so everyone was quiet, and their minds calmed down, and their five senses could work. At this time, they discovered the rattling sound of an airplane vibrating in the air. The sound gradually increased, and finally it sounded over their heads. Although this was a ravine, when they raised their heads, they could still see a seam of blue sky. At this time, the plane flew very low, swooping past the top of the mountain seam. (421)

"Name" and "Reality" 202

— Yang Yusheng

When Zhuge Jing was in Wu, during a grand court meeting, Sun Hao asked, "Your name is Zhongsi, what do you think about?" He replied, "At home, I think of filial piety, serving the ruler, I think of loyalty, friends, I think of faith, that's all!"

This is a pedantic talk that ordinary people today would disdain. But I must advise those who have the same status as Zhuge Jing not to use names that are too "magnificent," such as ritual, righteousness, integrity, and loyalty, because if you happen to meet a fool like Sun Hao, you might not be able to talk as loudly as Zhuge Jing!

Animals Forecast Weather 203

— Bing Yu

Today, science is flourishing, and the method of observing the weather is of course based on astronomy. However, in the era when science was not developed, the changes in the weather were predicted solely by the movements of animals. Among the animals, birds, beasts, insects, and fish, many can occupy the clear or rainy weather, based on the principles of meteorology, from the temperature, humidity, air pressure, and sunlight conditions, and have been repeatedly tested and proven. They are divided as follows:

Goldfish: If we use a goldfish tank that is one foot and five inches deep and six inches in diameter, pave the bottom of the tank with yellow sand, plant aquatic plants, fill the tank with eight-tenths of water, and put in two or three three-year-old goldfish, still follow the ordinary goldfish breeding method, without any difference, then we can judge the weather from the living conditions of the goldfish. For example, if you want to go out in the future, if you want to know if it will rain, you can see it in the goldfish tank. If the weather will be clear, the water in the fish tank contains enough oxygen, and the goldfish must be steadily and quietly submerged at the bottom of the tank. If the air gradually becomes humid, as if it is about to rain, the goldfish will have difficulty absorbing oxygen in the water, and will gradually float to the top, even stretching its mouth out of the water to absorb oxygen, and its breathing will be very rapid, then, after three or four hours, it will definitely rain. This method is most effective from May to October. However, the tank and the number of fish stocked must be in accordance with the above. If the tank is small and there are many fish, and no aquatic plants are planted, the weather cannot be predicted. (If the tank is small and there are many fish, the oxygen in the water cannot be supplied for life, and they will also float to the surface.) However, why should aquatic plants be planted at the bottom of the goldfish tank? It is not just for decoration, because aquatic plants are plants that absorb a large amount of air from outside the water, take nitrogen as their own nutrients, digest and absorb it, and release oxygen into the water. Therefore, no matter how high the water temperature rises, if the weather is not bad, the goldfish will still benefit from this oxygen, and even if the tank water is not changed, they will still live quietly submerged at the bottom of the water. Therefore, with the remedy of aquatic plants, they get a lot of oxygen. In the past, old fishermen used this goldfish weather forecast to infer the life of fish in rivers. In clear weather, fish must swim at the bottom of the water, and the fishing hook bait should be submerged at the bottom of the water. If it is about to rain, because the fish have difficulty breathing, they will float to the surface of the water, and the fishing hook bait should of course float on the surface. Thinking about it this way, raising goldfish can not only determine whether the weather is clear or rainy, but also serve as a guide for fishing.

Frogs: The sound of frogs croaking is most effective in relation to rain. According to the experiments of Mr. Maeda, director of the Osaka Meteorological Observatory in Japan, it will rain within 30 hours after a frog croaks. He experimented in the Obihiro area and got a score of 64%, in Wakayama, he got a score of 70%, and in Shiomisaki, he got a score of 52%. The average statistic is 62% effective, so the frog is also known as the rain frog.

Cats and Dogs: When a cat strokes its ears with its forelimbs (from behind the ears to the face), it is a sign that the weather will be clear. If both cats and dogs eat grass, it can be predicted that it will rain.

Chickens: If chickens wander around foraging non-stop from morning till night, it is a sign of rain.

Sparrows: If yellow sparrows bathe in the river, it is a sign of clear weather.

Swallows: If swallows dance high in the sky, it is a sign that the weather will be clear. Flying low in the sky and eagerly foraging for food is a sign of rain.

Ants: If termites come out, it is proof that the weather will continue to be unchanged.

Snakes: If snakes climb trees, it is a sign of rain.

Earthworms: If earthworms chirp, it is a sign of clear weather.

Promulgation of Regulations for People's Schools by the Ministry of Education 205

On June 26th, the Ministry of Education promulgated the following regulations for people's schools:

▲Regulations for People's Schools

Article 1: People's schools shall adhere to the educational objectives and implementation guidelines of the Republic of China, imparting simple knowledge and skills to illiterate adults. People's schools may establish advanced classes as needed.

Article 2: People's schools shall be established by townships, towns, neighborhoods, and various educational institutions, civic organizations, factories, and shops. Provincial, municipal, and county governments, district offices, and private individuals may also establish people's schools.

Article 3: The establishment, alteration, and closure of people's schools shall be reported to the competent educational administrative authorities for approval and record.

Article 4: People's schools shall annually prepare budget statements, accounting statements, and implementation plans, and submit them to the competent educational administrative authorities for examination and record.

Article 5: Within one month after the commencement of teaching in each class, people's schools shall prepare a register of teachers and staff, including their resumes and salaries, along with class rosters, teaching schedules, and lists of teaching materials, and submit them to the competent educational administrative authorities for record.

Article 6: All illiterate persons aged sixteen or above shall be admitted to people's schools. Those who have completed the courses of people's schools or possess equivalent qualifications may enter advanced classes. In areas where short-term compulsory education has not been implemented, illiterate persons aged ten or above may also be admitted to people's schools.

Article 7: The organization of classes in people's schools shall be based on learning ability. However, when necessary, classes may be divided by age and gender.

Article 8: People's schools shall not charge tuition or other fees. When funding is sufficient, they may also provide impoverished students with books and stationery.

Article 9: The total number of class hours for students in people's schools shall not be less than two hundred hours. For advanced class students, completion of the prescribed curriculum shall be the limit. The daily teaching time for people's schools shall be two hours in principle, and may be conducted during holidays or at night.

Article 10: Students who pass the final examination of people's schools shall be given a certificate of academic achievement by the school.

Article 11: After the completion of studies by students, people's schools shall prepare a register of each student's name, gender, age, place of origin, and academic achievements, and submit it to the competent educational administrative authorities for record.

Article 12: The subjects taught in people's schools shall be Mandarin (including civics and general knowledge), arithmetic (abacus or written calculation), music, and physical education. The subjects taught in advanced classes shall be Mandarin (including civics and general knowledge), arithmetic, music, physical education, and subjects related to occupations.

Article 13: Textbooks used in people's schools shall be those edited or approved by the Ministry of Education. People's schools may compile supplementary textbooks to adapt to the environment and needs.

Article 14: People's schools shall promote and implement extracurricular activities, which shall be determined by each school in accordance with local conditions and needs.

Article 15: People's schools shall have one principal and several teachers, who shall be qualified primary school teachers or have received training as instructors in popular education. If the principal is full-time, he/she shall also teach classes.

Article 16: Principals of people's schools established by provincial, municipal, and county governments shall be appointed by the provincial, municipal, and county educational administrative authorities. Principals of people's schools established by various levels of autonomous organizations, educational institutions, civic organizations, factories, shops, and private individuals shall be appointed by the establishers and reported to the competent educational administrative authorities for record. Teachers of people's schools shall be appointed by the principal.

Article 17: These regulations may be amended by the Ministry of Education when necessary.

Article 18: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Educational Associations of Various Counties in Jiangsu Unanimously Oppose the County Treasury System ▲ Undermines the Principle of Independent Educational Funding ▲ Telegram to the Central Government Requesting Strict Correction 212

The Jiangsu Provincial Government recently announced the County Treasury System, which, starting from July 1st, will unify the revenue and expenditure of various funds in each county, including educational funding, under the management of the County Treasury. The educational associations of Songjiang, Shanghai, and other counties, upon hearing this news, are deeply concerned that the principle of independent educational funding will be undermined, thus shaking the original educational undertakings. Therefore, they held a temporary discussion meeting at the Shanghai County Party Headquarters yesterday. More than twenty people attended, including Chen Guisan from Songjiang, Sun Jichu from Shanghai, Lu Yunqi from Jiading, Zhao Yancang from Qingpu, Zhao Shouheng from Kunshan, Lin Baoheng from Fengxian, and Zhao Xinmei from Nanhui. Sun Jichu was elected as the chairman, and Lu Yangzhou as the recorder. After the formalities, the chairman reported the main purpose of the meeting, followed by discussion on: (1) The County Treasury System promulgated by the Provincial Government's Finance Department this time incorporates educational funding into administrative expenses, undermining the principle of independent educational funding and affecting educational undertakings. How should the association strive to protect the independent educational funding? It was decided to send a telegram to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government's Nanchang Headquarters, the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Education, and the Provincial Party Headquarters for correction, and also to send a telegram to the Provincial Government's Education Department requesting a reconsideration at the Provincial Government meeting to change the method in order to maintain independent educational funding. (2) The telegram to be sent today should be printed and distributed to the educational associations of various counties throughout the province, requesting them to unite and strive together. (3) Please request the County Party Headquarters of each county to express their unanimous opinion. (4) The Wuxian Educational Association is requested to convene a joint meeting of the educational associations of various counties throughout the province before July 15. A resolution was passed. (5) The Jiading County submitted two drafts for discussion and resolution. A resolution was passed after amendment. (6) The drafts resolved today, the telegrams and letters should be printed and distributed by Shanghai County. A resolution was passed. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

▲ The Significance of Planning and Building the Field According to the city authorities, the significance of planning and building the sports field this time is quite profound. On the one hand, it promotes sports and strengthens the physical fitness of citizens. On the other hand, it strives for construction and assists the prosperity and joy of building a large Shanghai. Moreover, the Sports Association's sports field has been relocated to build the Zhongshan Hospital, which has a significant impact on sports undertakings. In the future, the prosperity of the city center and both parties can cooperate to share the responsibility of developing sports.

▲ Completion of the Project by July Next Year The project was originally scheduled to start construction at the beginning of this month, and then continue to build a library and museum. However, the issuance of public bonds must wait for the final approval of the Legislative Yuan, so it has to be postponed slightly. However, in the shortest possible time, it should be able to start construction. Chengtai Factory won the bid with 878,203 yuan, but in any case, it must be completed before July next year so that the next National Games can be held in the field as scheduled. All decorations and arrangements will strive for magnificence and greatness.

Jews Allowed to Participate in the World Arylmpics ▲ German Representative Issues Statement ▲ Women's Participation Events Decided 224

(Reuters, London Dispatch) At the World Arylmpics General Assembly held in Athens, the German representative issued a statement saying that all German Jews will not only be allowed to participate in the World Arylmpics, but will also be allowed to represent Germany in the competition and receive absolute equal treatment with other athletes.

This Jewish issue was raised by the British representative with the support of the American representative, requesting a guarantee.

The Assembly also decided that women can participate in track and field, swimming, skating, and fencing events.

Finance: Silver Prices and Exchange Rates Rise Together 235

Spot Gold Price Falls Again by $4.50. High Prices Lead to Supply Exceeding Demand, Signs of a Rebound After Weakness. Banks Closed for Settlement on July 2nd and 3rd. 236

The gold market continued to decline yesterday due to the simultaneous rise in silver prices and exchange rates. At one point, the market became extremely weak due to rumors circulating about silver. However, major players bought during the dip, and banks also actively purchased at the lower prices. Signs of a rebound appeared after the decline. Early in the morning, overseas silver markets in England and America both rose, and the futures silver price on the Five Metals Exchange also rose by 0.18 to 0.41 cents. Exchange rates increased across the board. London spot gold fell by one penny, American cotton fell by nine basis points, American wheat remained unchanged, and stock prices experienced minor fluctuations. The tentative opening price retreated to a strong $8, but then rose due to more active buying during the dip. After the opening, although banks were keen to purchase, market sentiment was weak, and the domestic market tended to loosen. The market situation seemed weak. At one point, major players strongly supported purchases, which were quite effective in preventing further decline. Later, upon learning of the HSBC exchange rate listing, the British exchange rate rose by 1.25 and the American exchange rate rose by 3.75, triggering intense selling pressure and causing the price to retreat. However, it did not break the $8 mark, leading to bargain hunting. Major players also made strong purchases. The gold market suddenly rebounded. After entering the market, banks' appetite waned, and Sassoon strongly covered bills, causing the domestic market to continue to harden. Sellers asserted their dominance, breaking the $80 mark. Although there was a pull-up, ultimately, the Reuters report stating that the US Internal Revenue Committee instructed silver brokers with long positions to have their customers swear and fill out explanations did not have a significant impact. Furthermore, the US Congressman Dies announced that he would propose a bill in the next Congress to reduce the silver content of currency from 412.5 to 206 grains, similar to reducing the gold content, and also proposed restoring the old gold-silver ratio of 16 to 1 to replace the current 27 to 1. The gold market fell further, but stabilized due to banks taking advantage of the low prices to purchase. A report from the Seattle night market stated that the silver price had decreased by 0.25 and increased by 1.25, boosting market sentiment and pushing the price back above $80. However, the supply side was still eager to sell at the higher prices, causing it to decline. The bank market was very good. Reuters reported that the US government had decided to engage in a large-scale silver purchasing campaign, buying 135.4 million ounces in the next six months. The gold market remained high but still experienced a slight decline. In the after-market, although the Seattle night market silver price rose by 0.25, remained unchanged, and rose by 1.25, the price once retreated below $80. However, due to the banks' strong appetite, it gradually rose, and the market situation stabilized. The price of pure gold was calculated at $990.70. The day's market situation is recorded below:
