The Unstoppable Rise in Grain Prices 247

After the opening of the flour market this morning, the prices of each month showed a sharp and frantic trend. The quoted price of foreign wheat, Chicago, was good by 4 cents to 1 jiao, and Canada was less than 48 cents. However, recently, people in the market have paid less attention to foreign situations. The biggest focus at present is the drought in various places, the damage to the fields, and the influence on rice prices. As a result, attention has turned to the crazy purchase of flour and wheat, and the opening of traffic in North China is considered to be the way to restore the three eastern provinces. Whether the facts will be like this in the future has not been considered during the fever. Therefore, after the opening price, the near and far months have risen one after another. For example, November jumped wildly to 2 yuan 3 jiao, which is rarely justified when wheat is harvested. By the afternoon opening, the frenzy was still seen, but with extreme increases, some of the profitable speculative bulls took advantage of the trend to return to the market. It was rumored that it rained in North China, Wuxi rice returned to 2 jiao, paddy returned to 2 jiao, and wheat was 5 cents less, so people's hearts have turned weak. The repeated high prices will lead to the arrival of foreign flour wheat in China, which is possible as in the past two or three years. As a result, this month and July are still up 3 cents, August to October are each good by 2 cents and 7.5 li, and November is good by 1 cent and 7.5 li.

Another report Yesterday, the red sun was still in the sky, and off-market speculation was still high. However, after this surge, it is a huge obstacle for the flour in this port to be transported to the eastern provinces. It is heard that Australian flour can be ordered for 2 yuan and 8 jiao, and there is no problem without adding foreign flour tax to the eastern provinces. Although South China has tariff protection, the way of suicide is the same now and in the past. Therefore, although the drought has a reason to raise prices, it is also necessary to understand the domestic and foreign situation. However, at present, during the speculative frenzy, there is no way to talk about accurate speculation.

It is Said 251

— Yu

It is said that a good chess move is equivalent to several moves. A gentleman of the country does not do one-sided transactions. The effect should be unexpected, and the benefit lies in many aspects. For example, when buying something for one yuan, you can also eat a free box of ice cream, or get an aviation lottery ticket, with the hope of winning 500,000 yuan, which is a pleasure.

This is a wonderful way of doing many things at once. A shrew scolding in the street points at A, scolds B, is scolded by C, and makes D suffer, while also expressing herself. This kind of Tao is broad and profound. No wonder the autumn man of the past had the "art of scolding people", a great masterpiece.

The recent "scientific spiritual divination" is a great invention and a brilliant move. Are you superstitious about Western science? Please see the scientific spiritual divination. If you despise spiritual divination, then you must also disbelieve science; it increases the momentum of spiritual divination, and those who promote new culture will be unlucky, but poisonous domestic goods! Moreover, it will soon spread throughout China, and may even last for a long time. That power is far more powerful than a knife or a pen.

Doesn't society ridicule certain people as "eight-sided darlings"? Take a look at the social celebrities, entertaining guests, and being considerate in every aspect, and you can get a glimpse or two. But don't misunderstand that they are busy talking with eight tongues, but rather saying a word that makes eight people feel personally close and satisfied. There is a kind of ball game in the West where one ball knocks down eight or nine pins, which can describe this skill.

But why are there so few successful people of the "eight-sided darling" type? Because it is neither a Tao, nor are there many purposes, so the power is dispersed. If the power is divided, the result is weak. To prevent attacks from all sides, the result is only to be smooth and become a crystal ball. On the other hand, the sharp edges cannot be covered everywhere, and it ends in failure. On the contrary, perseverance, breaking the complex with the simple, is easy to achieve results. What's more, the way of man is endless, doesn't even a national chess player lose sometimes?

I Also Discuss the Controversy of Literary Language and Vernacular 252

— Jiang Qi

Since Mr. Wang Maozu and Mr. Wu Renyin started the controversy between literary language and vernacular, it has aroused the attention of the general public to a problem that was not originally a problem; especially the colleagues in the Shanghai literary circle, such as Mr. Chen Wangdao, Chen Zizhan, Cao Juren, Le Sibing, and Hu Yuzhi, have all published their opinions in this journal; it is said that there are still many people preparing manuscripts. However, most of the opinions they have published are based on the standpoint of the entire society, discussing how to popularize and make the tool of language universal, so that the general public, regardless of the wise, the mediocre, and the foolish, can understand and exchange opinions. Therefore, some of them have proposed creating a "mass language." Because I have been entrusted by them, they want me to participate with some opinions: now I will tentatively narrow the scope, stand solely on the position of education, and bring up the question of whether the first-grade Chinese textbook in elementary schools, especially in elementary schools, should use literary language or vernacular for discussion.

Of course, on Mr. Wang's side, he did not advocate that the first grade of elementary school must adopt literary language and should not adopt vernacular. He only advocated that school education should increase with the grade, from vernacular to both vernacular and literary language, and can completely adopt literary language in the university era. In this way, then, in the first grade of elementary school, whether it is Mr. Wang, Mr. Wu, or the gentlemen of the Shanghai literary world, they all unanimously advocate the adoption of vernacular, so there is no need for any controversy. The current problem lies only in how the first-grade Chinese textbook in elementary schools should be compiled. Specifically, what kind of vernacular should it adopt to be correct? Because Mr. Hu Yuzhi pointed out that there are several types of vernacular: such as the vernacular after the May Fourth Movement, the quotations style, the Saturday School, and the Zhang Henshui School, and even the "mass language" proposed by Mr. Chen Zizhan, etc. Therefore, the content of the first-grade Chinese textbook in elementary schools in the future has become a problem as to what vernacular should be used. However, I personally do not want to or am not able to express any opinions on this issue at the moment. What I want to say is that I have to temporarily borrow the first volume of the Japanese elementary school Chinese textbook to examine it and see how the Japanese side views this issue, and then write out the results of my review for the reference of my country's educators.

The Japanese elementary school Chinese textbooks have always been used in combination with Kana and Kanji. Needless to say, the Chinese textbooks in the higher grades of elementary school are like this, even the Chinese textbooks in the first grade of elementary school, except for the very first one or two pages which are all in Kana, at least there is always one or two or three Kanji on the remaining pages, and the more pages there are, the more Kanji there are. As for now, please take the first volume of the elementary school Chinese textbook for ordinary courses issued by the Ministry of Education in December of Showa 7 to read, and it is not difficult to find that the Japanese textbooks have been greatly reformed. Specifically, although the first volume of the Japanese elementary school Chinese textbook still uses Kana and Kanji in combination, the number of Kanji characters is very few. There is not a single Kanji from the first page to the twenty-fifth page, all in Kana; then Kanji such as "一" (one), "二" (two), "三" (three), "四" (four) are inserted on the twenty-sixth page; from the twenty-seventh page to the thirtieth page are all in Kana again; Kanji such as "山" (mountain), "川" (river), "小" (small), "木" (tree), "五" (five) are inserted on the fortieth page; after that, there is only one Kanji "大" (big) on the forty-second page, and Kanji such as "六" (six), "七" (seven), "八" (eight), "九" (nine), "十" (ten) on the forty-fourth page; on the forty-fifth page, the numbers from "一" (one) to "十" (ten) are re-mentioned, and the Kanji on the forty-sixth and forty-seventh pages are only re-mentioning the Kanji that have been presented in the previous pages, such as "木" (tree), "山" (mountain). Later, the character "日" (sun) is presented on the forty-eighth page, the character "目" (eye) is presented on the fiftieth page, the character "中" (middle) is presented on the fifty-seventh page, the character "犬" (dog) is presented on the sixtieth page, the character "上" (up) is presented on the sixty-seventh page, and the character "人" (person) is presented on the seventy-second page. Apart from this, no other Kanji are presented. In total, there are seventy-eight pages in this mountain language textbook, and the number of Kanji characters occupied in it is only twenty-one characters such as "一, 二, 三, 四, 五, 六, 七, 八, 九, 十, 山, 川, 小, 木, 大, 日, 目, 中, 犬, 上, 人"; moreover, these twenty-one Kanji characters are only the concepts of numbers and very superficial concepts commonly used in daily life. From this, it can be seen that Japanese education is showing a tendency to reduce the number of Kanji characters as much as possible and emphasize the use of Kana more. It is also not known whether it will completely abandon Kanji and use Kana exclusively in the future. I dare to assert that this tendency of Japan is by no means due to the so-called education policy of "preserving national essence," but is based on the advocacy of new pedagogy.

If this proposition of Japan is correct, then the problem of Chinese textbooks in elementary schools in our country in the future is not a controversy between literary language and vernacular, but a question of whether to adopt "phonetic alphabet" or "phonetic symbols." This problem is also very huge, and I am not in a position to interfere. I will leave it to the educational administrative authorities to solve it themselves.

(Written in Shanghai on June 24, 23)

Random Notes from Mandalay 253

— Liu Ming

(1) In savage places, the words "fellow villager" still have considerable use; but in civilized cities, it is not so. For example, in Mandalay, the old capital of Burma, if you don't know the streets when you first go there, and you are hesitating to step into the midst of the traffic, and you ask a passing Chinese person for directions, then you will most likely hear the following Burmese reply:

"Nan Men Le Bu."

Meaning that I don't understand what you are saying, and then the person walks away with a straight face. Perhaps recognizing fellow villagers will more easily cause other troubles: such as asking for temporary help, entrusting to find work. Therefore, the words "fellow villager" are like rotten fruit in the summer, and cannot be sold at a good price here.

On the other hand, some Muslim Indian shopkeepers who know a little Chinese will learn the accent of the Yunnan people and greet you very kindly when you pass by their shops:

"Fellow villager, come in and take a look. If you don't buy, it's okay."

Comparing these two, one can glean another meaning from between people.

(2)

Burma, this country of coconuts and durians, I imagined as having a lot of romantic atmosphere during the trip; but once I arrived in Mandalay, on the ferry of the Irrawaddy River, looking at the wing of the green mountains on the east bank, in the misty rain, sending countless white pagodas, and the next morning, wearing a robe and looking out the window, seeing the monks in yellow robes, appearing in teams on the streets flooded with morning light, it gave people a sense of solemnity.

However, it doesn't make people feel gloomy, probably because they are not as rigid as we Chinese. For example, ordinary monks can eat fish and meat every day, and they also have freedom of love. Because, if they fall in love with a young female believer, or the daughter of a benefactor, they can take off their cassock and return to secular life. This has been the case with them since ancient times, and no one will criticize it.

Therefore, asceticism and indulgence do not conflict much in this country: just living in Mandalay for two or three days, you will deeply feel this atmosphere.

(3)

"Tengyue Hall Chronicle" records the previous situation in Mandalay: "There is a brick city around, sixty-two li, with twelve gates, and wooden fences are set up outside, prohibiting rapid riding." When I saw it, the wooden fence was gone, and rapid riding was not prohibited, because there were already two shiny rails stretching into the city gate without any ceremony. Cannons were set up on the city tower, and foreign soldiers in yellow twill uniforms guarded the side all day long.

The style of the city wall is full of Chinese style, and it is said that it was built by Chinese craftsmen hired by the Burmese king in the past. The age seems not too long ago, and the characteristics that a general ancient city should have: incompleteness, plus the decoration of vines, none of those exist.

Outside the city, "the south is Chinatown, with many Chinese traders. The west is the foreign street, with a total of seventy-two streets, large and small." This was the situation in the eleventh year of Guangxu. If we trace back to before there was Chinatown and the foreign street, I think the situation of the market must be very interesting. "Diannan Magazine" records that under the Burmese king "there are four great wan, followed by wan tao, and outside of that there are seven wan." "Each wan has no salary, and they are ordered to do business, to take profit as official capital." From this point of view, being an official and being a boss have become inseparable things, then the government and the store are either merged into one, or they are next to each other.

Cloud Rainbow 254

— TK

Elopement ㈢ 255

— Written by Petőfi of Hungary, Translated by Shi Yongyi

'Now you are mine, Anna丨丨 all of you丨丨 all of you丨This beautiful brunette hair, red and sweet cherry lips, passionate and dark eyes, proud and swan-like neck丨丨, all belong to me.'

'Yes丨丨 Yes丨丨 I belong to you, Karl!'

They were happy丨丨 not for long. But sensual love is a kind of intoxication, and when they woke up from this intoxication and recovered their senses, they couldn't help but shout:

'What will we live on? We have no money! We have nothing to eat.'

Before they could finish speaking, someone was knocking at the door. Then an unknown person walked in.

'May I have the honor of saying a few words to Mr. Karl?'

Karl heard this, confused and panicked, because he felt that he had met that person before.

'You don't answer,' the unknown person continued, 'but the panic in your words has already proved that you are the person I want to visit. I ask you to sign this small piece of paper. I will come to visit you again a year from today. Don't forget丨丨 exactly one year. Goodbye.'

This mysterious man left. But at this time, it is difficult to say which was stronger, the panic or the joy of this couple. Because the piece of paper that the unknown person gave him was a check for an amount sufficient to provide them with a year of luxurious living. According to the way it was written, payable on sight, the money could be paid to them immediately.

'This is incomprehensible,' Mrs. Anna said, looking at the check.

'This is really inexplicable.' Karl agreed. 'Gold is falling to us, just like heavenly dew.'

Now they can live a very happy life. They will not be subjected to material oppression. Now they think that the merchant certainly does not know them. If he did, why didn't he tell Andro?

'At the end of the year,' Karl said, 'this unknown person will come again, and we will have more money. Didn't he say that?'

'Yes.'

Questions About the People's Language 256

— Stupid

Before I wrote this rubbish, I have a few statements to make. I fundamentally do not understand how to make the people's language, and I don't even understand what kind of writing the people's language is. Because I see that the few writers who advocate the people's language are just scolding literary Chinese and vernacular Chinese in a roundabout way, and as a result, they have not announced how to make the people's language and how to make it easy to popularize. It is really "a tall monk of two meters, unable to touch his head." And after carefully reading the writings of the writers who advocate the people's language, I can't smell the flavor of the people's language at all. It is still the tone of the Lan Qing Mandarin. It can be seen everywhere, so I fundamentally do not understand what the people's language is all about, so I want to ask for advice.

If you gentlemen are willing to give sincere advice with an attitude of consultation, I will be very welcome. If you come and scold me in a roundabout way, "old stubborn," "reversing the car," "anti-era," "outdated," and other titles will be conferred on me all at once, I can only cover my mouth and remain silent, letting you scold me severely. I will never dare to hum or open my mouth again. This is a lesson I have learned from decades of experience.

Speaking of writing, the old antiques of the past, which were conceived in the womb, should not be taken out again. Let's talk about the most recent writing first. Since the beginning of the Republic of China, the writing commonly used in our country can be divided into about four types.

One type is the old-fashioned literary Chinese.

One type is newspaper-style writing.

One type is translation-style writing (or it can be called Europeanized writing).

One type is the commonly called vernacular Chinese (or spoken language).

I am bringing these out, which seems to have nothing to do with this issue, but it can be understood that the changes in writing have a sense of the times and a sense of evolution. Among these four types of writing, the old-fashioned literary Chinese is not suitable for use and is aristocratic, so let's put it aside for now. Secondly, let's talk about newspaper-style writing. This type of writing has both vernacular and literary Chinese. If you add a few more "的" (de) or "呢" (ne) characters, it can be said to be vernacular Chinese. If you refine and polish it a little more, it can also be said to be literary Chinese. Next, let's talk about translation-style writing. Because the writing translated by several Western scholars and degree holders such as Yan Youling and Lin Qinnan was too obscure and difficult to understand, they changed their style and used vernacular to translate. Because the Chinese and Western languages are ultimately different in sentence structure (foreign languages put the main words in front and the subsidiary words behind, while Chinese puts the subsidiary words in front and the main words behind. One is deductive, and one is inductive. This can be seen on Chinese and Western envelopes). The translated writing is often more than a chopstick long, and there are two or three or more "的" (de) characters in it. This is called translation-style writing. And then there is the vernacular Chinese advocated by several writers after the New Culture Movement.

Among these four types of writing, the old-fashioned literary Chinese is rarely used except in official documents and birthday prefaces. Because the translation-style writing is not understood by readers, the sentences have also gradually shortened. Only newspaper writing

Page 20

and vernacular Chinese are now very powerful and unimpeded. However, some people have also advocated that newspaper writing should be changed to vernacular, but because of various obstacles and the fact that vernacular Chinese occupies too much space, it has not been implemented. Perhaps this is the shortcoming of vernacular Chinese. As for vernacular writing, it has not been promoted for long, and there are still some people who come out to oppose it. From this point of view, in terms of vernacular Chinese itself, it has not yet reached a stable stage, and it has not yet reached a perfect stage. Now some people are advocating the people's language. In fact, the reason why the current vernacular Chinese cannot be completely unimpeded and there are still people who stand up to oppose and destroy it may also be because the vernacular Chinese has not yet reached a perfect state. We should first study and sort out the vernacular Chinese. If it really cannot be improved, then we can advocate other types of writing. If we do not study or research because the vernacular Chinese still has difficult places, and we overthrow and destroy it, and then advocate a kind of people's language, I think this kind of progress is too rapid, isn't it? The occurrence and success of any event always has a sense of the times and a sense of evolution. It is impossible to cross to the thirty-third heaven in one step.

I will clarify such an evolution first, and then talk about the people's language. I generally observe that the writers who advocate the people's language mostly advocate adopting slang, and extremely common slang. This meaning is indeed very good. I think it will definitely be a bit difficult to implement, because the dialects in various places are mostly different. If the people of Jiangsu think it is popular, but people elsewhere may not understand it. For example, the Ningbo people's "阿拉" (ala) and the Suzhou people's "裏篤" (li du), people who often live in Shanghai think it is popular, but if people in Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou hear it, they still don't understand it.

In fact, slang and literary Chinese all depend on whether they can be used universally or not. If slang is used to, it can become literary Chinese. If literary Chinese is used to, it can become slang. It all depends on getting used to it. If it is used for a long time, it will naturally become common. Therefore, at the beginning of advocating the people's language, we cannot immediately turn all literary Chinese into slang. In the beginning, we can only use both literary Chinese and slang. To put it bluntly, we should use some literary Chinese and some vernacular. Over time, it may be possible to turn it completely into slang. There is no reason to reach the goal in one step.

I see that some writers, as soon as they see someone occasionally use a literary Chinese word, say that he is not thorough enough. This is too excessive. For example, if a case of patricide occurs in Hubei Province, they say that all the people in Hubei Province are patricides. If a case of robbery occurs in Anhui Province, they say that all the people in Anhui Province are robbers. Isn't this a joke? In fact, vernacular Chinese only has three conditions, which are the most important: can be written, can be spoken, and can be understood. In the past, during the Qing Dynasty, some people also advocated unifying the national language. What method should be used to unify this national language? Only by selecting a literary Chinese as the standard language. Therefore, at that time, there was a great debate in the Executive Yuan. Some advocated using Henan language, because Luoyang is in the center of China, so the Central Plains language should be adopted as the standard. Some advocated using Beijing language, because Beijing is the capital, so the Beijing language should be adopted as the standard. As a result of the debate between the two sides, the victory naturally belonged to the latter (because my brain is very bad, there may be errors in time, but there is always such a fact). Unified to the present, although there are still few people who can speak real Mandarin, there are many who can speak and understand Lan Qing Mandarin. I think that if the writers who advocate the people's language also take being able to write, hear, and speak as conditions, no matter how Lan Qing it is, as long as people can understand it, write it, and speak it, that's it. Why bother to seek other methods? If there are still some inappropriate places in the current vernacular Chinese, it is more convenient to improve the vernacular Chinese first. I don't know what the writers who advocate the people's language think of my opinion.

"High Expectations" 257

June 29, 28, 27

Reading "My Ideal Future Life Special Issue" 258

— He Juefu

丨Women's World No. 19丨

Everyone is bound to have dreams. Living a hard life can also be said to be looking forward to and pursuing future dreams; if human beings have no dreams, they may die from it.

Dreams are originally real and free in one's own mind; but when they are written on white paper, there will inevitably be some hypocrisy and affectation; the reason is that speaking when one is conscious, one cannot but take into account all aspects of the human world. In "My Ideal Future Life Special Issue", these female authors who tell their dreams, to what extent their hypocrisy and affectation are, cannot be deduced now, so let's assume that they are completely true.

These eleven young women who have received higher education, some are looking forward to finding an ideal lover and living the life of a virtuous wife and loving mother; some are longing for the beauty of nature and want to live a leisurely life in a secluded village with beautiful mountains and clear waters; some are seeking a suitable job to avoid relying on others for support and enduring their restraints; some feel that the current situation in China is so chaotic and the status of women in society is so low, and want to dedicate themselves to the country and fight for themselves. Although the dreams they talk about are so different; but in the final analysis, most of them are still fascinated by the personal "enjoyable, poetic life."

In China, women who have received higher education can also be said to be the most advanced and most awakened. For thousands of years, they have been tightly bound by the old morality and old etiquette, and have been like lambs succumbing to the authority of their husbands. In recent decades, due to the collapse of the old system and the struggle of many awakened people, a part has escaped from the old shackles; but as soon as they get rid of the old restraints, the new professional chains are tightly hanging on their necks. Isn't the matter of selling one's appearance everywhere? Isn't the cry of "vase" everywhere to be heard? Tens of thousands of poor women are eager for these advanced and awakened same-sex people to support and rescue them, but these advanced and awakened people are single-mindedly ignoring them and fascinated by pink dreams, which is not to make people sigh!

After reading this special issue, a terrible shadow appeared in my mind about the future of the women's movement; my only hope is that the dreams said are completely false and pretentious!

The Heroic Collective Suicide of Nine Women 260

— Naifu

The Shen Bao's special telegram on the 24th said: "Seven sisters-in-law and aunts from the same Pan surname family outside the North Gate of Hui'an, Fujian, and two from the Chen surname, nine women formed an alliance and committed suicide. On the 21st night, they tied each other into a formation and jumped into the water, all died. The women are aged thirteen to nineteen, married or unmarried, except for the youngest one, most of them were dissatisfied with their marriages and tired of the world." After reading this news, we can't help but feel terrified and really feel "What world is this?" "Is it real or a dream?"

But as long as we have a little memory and a little reason, we can unhesitatingly determine that this is completely true, not a "dream" at all. This is a phenomenon that is bound to occur in the current Chinese society, and there is no need to be surprised!

The more social systems move towards an inevitable decline, the more cruel they become. Because the other side of the decline of the old society is the rise of the new society. The more rapid the process of decline, the more intense the confrontation between the old and the new will be. When it reaches a certain point, the old will be discarded and the new will be produced at the same time.

Historically speaking, China's feudal patriarchal system should be in decline now. But the facts tell us that its cruelty is getting worse day by day. The suicide of Mrs. Qin Lizhai and her children and the whole family earlier this month had already exposed the evils of this outdated system to the world. This collective suicide of nine women especially shows a heroic and tragic social phenomenon. They are major phenomena with historical significance; not accidental events worthy of pity; not their cowardly and humble acts; but a heroic and tragic act!

On the same day, the Shen Bao also published a news item about a female student from Hangzhou Girls' High School who also committed suicide due to marriage problems, which further proves that this type of phenomenon is common everywhere in China. What's more, in the closed areas of the interior, which are also the places where the patriarchal system is most powerful, I don't know how many similar events are happening in various ways, and are ultimately covered up by the strong forces of ghosts and gods and various means, and cannot be seen in the newspapers and attract everyone's attention.

Speaking of this, I cannot but loudly appeal to my enlightened Chinese women: The promotion of history depends entirely on human power. Women account for half of humanity, and naturally bear half of the mission for the future of mankind. Moreover, all the poisons that the old society has given to women are even worse than those given to men. According to the principle that the greater the oppression, the stronger the resistance, the resistance of women should be stronger than that of men! If the oppression is too heavy, it is better to commit suicide happily than to endure suffering and steal life. But suicide must have some meaning. If you die in vain, what is the meaning of death?

Third-Class Ward 261

— Ya Fei

In a simple third-class ward, six beds are arranged lengthwise and crosswise. In front of each bed, there is a small square table, on which rests a teapot and a spittoon. The air inside is very silent, except for the coughing and moaning of a few patients, there is almost no sign of life!

When I was sent to the ×× Hospital, my nerves were unusually disordered, so I knew nothing; after being put to sleep on a small white-painted iron bed against the wall, a smell of foul medicine rushed to my brain. At that moment, I regained my lost senses.

It was nighttime. I turned over in bed, opened my eyes, and looked around, and everything surprised me. The faces in the room were all unfamiliar, and I couldn't recognize any of them at all. My Mei was missing, and I couldn't find my mother and brother either. I wanted to ask the person sleeping in the other bed, but I didn't dare. So, the words I wanted to say several times were finally swallowed back into my stomach, and my heart was indeed a little frustrated!

In the center of the room, the ten-candlepower electric light emitted its dim light, which was so bleak that it had no strength at all. It was just like the patients in bed.

In the corridor outside the door, clear, rhythmic footsteps came from outside in bursts. Then, the door opened, and a young woman in plain clothes walked in, holding a tray. Smiling, she approached the bed and placed the tray on the small square table. First, she took my pulse and measured my temperature. Then, she took the pulse and measured the temperature of everyone else in the same way.

"How are your bowel movements? Can you sleep?" Everyone was asked this question as a matter of course.

Testing stool, testing urine, testing blood, testing sputum. These are the initial procedures that every patient must undergo when they arrive at the hospital.

Old Su and Old Li have been living here for more than half a year. They used to live in the second-class ward, but later they moved to this third-class ward because of economic reasons.

According to them: they used to contact the night nurses every night, secretly running out to watch movies, go to hotels and gamble. In fact, their illnesses had long been cured, but because they didn't cherish their bodies, they are now worse, and the problems are more serious than before!

They can't be so free now. This is because the treatment in the third-class ward is certainly not as good as in the first and second classes. Now, after they have eaten dinner, they are taken to the chapel to listen to a sermon about Jesus; when they can't sleep after returning, they open their throats and tell stories from "Shan Hai Jing," "Jianghu Qi Xia Zhuan," "Jin Gu Qi Guan," etc. These are their best materials. However, they have to keep their voices especially low, because if it's too loud, it will affect other people's sleep and they will be interfered with by the nurses. But I don't feel too lonely because of this.

During the daytime, 9 a.m. to 12 noon is the best time to rest. Temperature is measured three times a day, pulse is taken three times, and medicine is taken three times. All life is mechanized. After lunch, one must take a bath and wipe the body. After these things are done, one prepares to stretch one's neck and hope that relatives, friends, and family will come to visit.

Every visiting hour, the elevator is crowded with people visiting patients. Especially me, whenever someone comes to visit me, I always reluctantly ask them to sit for a while longer. When they leave, I stare blankly at the door and feel sad for a while!

This situation is like a prisoner in jail hoping that acquaintances will come to visit him.

I only stayed in the ×× Hospital for more than a month; however, it almost destroyed my entire soul and burned my active life to death. Although the smiles and consolation of the young women in plain clothes are worth cherishing, they cannot eliminate my frustration and cannot hide my sadness! So, I finally couldn't wait to get well and made an excuse to leave the third-class ward and go to the countryside to recuperate.

The countryside has a quiet environment and fresh air, which is most suitable for patients to recuperate. Moreover, I am a "wild child" who is active by nature and doesn't like to be quiet. Being locked up in that innocent prison like in a hospital, unable to step out of the ward! It was simply suffocating me!

However, when I left the lovely young women in plain clothes and stepped onto the Shanghai-Hangzhou train, I still looked back at the roof of the hospital and shouted in a low voice: "Farewell! My lovely young women in plain clothes!"

### Good-for-Nothing Son 262

— Han Bai

Father's dim and old face has become increasingly gloomy lately!

The hardworking and simple father gives all the harvest, the remaining wealth, accumulated and saved from his labor of a drop of blood and a drop of sweat, to his son to send him to a commercial university.

He丨丨the father endures all the pain, all the insults and ridicule. In the severe winter, people wear brand new fur coats, but he still wears a cotton robe made of coarse cloth; in the hot summer, people wear soft and light summer clothes, but he still wears a heavy cloth garment. However, on the outside, he always looks so happy and joyful, because all his happiness, hope, and comfort are entrusted to his son's future. Zheng Daihe's works

He hopes that after his son finishes his studies, he can become a high official, or at least make a lot of money, to compensate for the price he paid before, to breathe a breath of free air, and to show off his power in front of people. After all, his past endurance has been rewarded.

But his son cannot repay his ardent wishes. His son has been away from the diploma exchange university for almost two years, and he is still the same son as before, except that his face is a little older and his beard is a little thicker. Wandering and drifting in the bustling city, he is rejected outside the iron circle of the current society. He has not learned the art of being an official, the skill of making money; nor does he have powerful relatives or money to curry favor. In this way, he can never have official luck in the current society, no matter how his father boasts that his son's fate is noble, the result is only to disappoint him!

Because his son is an extraordinary son (of course, in his father's opinion, a good-for-nothing son), a son with reason. How could he not know how eagerly his father hoped that he could bring glory to his ancestors; how could he not know how his father had struggled to get the money to provide for him to study. Perhaps he understood these issues even better than his father. He knew very well that money, which is used as a measure for exchanging goods, can enslave and trample on everyone, but he never wanted to be a prisoner of money. On the contrary, he wanted to destroy the money that can enslave people. He forgot all tiredness and lived his hard life rationally and painfully. He believes that the family is a local problem, and the dregs of individualism should be eliminated from the family first.

And his father? He has been left far behind by the wheels of the times! The poison he has received from feudal society is too deep! If the consciousness of all mankind were the same as his father's, then the structure of the current society would be as stable as Mount Tai, and the people in the palaces and dance halls could always tranquilly dream sweet dreams and enjoy their unique honor.

Living in these two extremely opposite worlds, naturally his father can only sigh, roar, and scold his son as a good-for-nothing son with disappointed eyes!

Amateur Mailbox

### No Trace 263

Editor:

Not long ago, I saw an advertisement in the "Shishi Xinbao" for a free sample of the "Golden Arrow" pen nib, saying that it was exquisite and beautiful, and no pen nib could match it. It would never break the paper, whether writing Chinese or Western characters. There was also a sample coupon printed in the newspaper, which said: "Cut out the coupon, write the sender's address and name, and send it to Post Office Box 1567 with a ten-cent sample coupon. After receiving it, we will send it immediately." But after several days, there was no trace, not a single message. Recently, I wrote him another letter, asking him if he had received it, but there has been no information so far. The ten-cent postage stamp is a trivial matter, but I don't understand what kind of trick they are playing. Please help me solve this problem? With kind regards,

Sincerely, Hu Kan

Answer: I don't know what the content of the question you asked is. Does this advertisement for a free sample have a brand name or company address printed on it in the newspaper? If not, it is a bit suspicious. According to my guess, the reason why you sent the sample coupon and there was no trace is probably due to three reasons. First, the letter was not delivered. Second, the store is slow to handle things and has not yet sent the sample. Third, it is a scam to defraud money. Since you remember the address so clearly, it is unlikely that it was not delivered by the post office. Moreover, it has been many days since you sent it. No matter how slow the handling is, there should always be a reply. Therefore, it is likely that you have been deceived in sending the postage stamp to ask for the pen nib this time. Nowadays, many of these advertisements that attract readers to buy by saying "attach a few cents of postage, and we will send it immediately" are scams. Therefore, we should not completely trust formal advertisements that do not publish the company's numbers and addresses, but only say to send letters to a certain mailbox. There is no such thing as a free lunch in the world. Being greedy for small gains is the easiest way to be fooled. Editor

Fiction

### Chastity Widow Arch (14) 264

— Ling He

Many years passed from then on. When this chastity widow died in her eighty-sixth year, she told her son in her will:

"∶∶∶Go and ask Uncle Fengxiang to write my epitaph. Kneel in front of him and ask him to include the matter of the candle sticks.∶∶∶"

In this way, Madam Shi's secret was revealed from Grandfather Fengxiang's mouth, and this was how she became a chastity widow. As for building the stone archway and requesting the imperial decree, that upright family uncle spent a lot of effort. At that time, he had already served as the chief examiner once. Counting it, it has been forty years since then. However, that chief examiner has been dead for many years, leaving only his son who made a fortune and lives ten miles away from the village. This is something everyone knows.

I don't know when it started, but hot winds have risen in the gaps between the leaves. When a black cloud floats past the sun, a shadow immediately follows and crawls across the ground, but it disappears in a moment, until the second cloud floats past.

When Shi Min woke up, his father was returning from the city. He had gone to the city this morning, and according to his usual habit, he would not be home until after the sun went down. But he came back especially early, which inevitably made his mother express surprise and ask:

"Why are you back so early today? It's not dark yet."

"What's so strange about that?" the father said frankly. "Of course I'll come back early if there's nothing to do. ∶∶∶Let me tell you, today I met someone from the provincial capital in the county who said that Huang Xing is agitating for revolution again, and I'm afraid there will be changes in the overall situation in China. But the newspaper didn't report it."

"Oh? Then how did that person know?" the mother said, watching her father take off his long gown.

"If there really is such a thing," the father said with concern as he unbuttoned his short shirt, "then the fate of the Manchus is about to end. From the time Emperor Shunzhi entered the pass to now, it has been more than three hundred years. But from Emperor Guangxu to now, two generations in a row cannot pass on the legitimate line. It was already strange that Tongzhi passed the throne to his younger brother Guangxu, and now Xuantong wants to inherit from two ancestors with one word. Then the palace maids and concubines cannot even give birth to a son. Isn't this Heaven ending their line?"
